After 25 charge–discharge cycles, both materials contain a noticeable amount of KClO<sub>4</sub>. b) Part of the XRD patterns of K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O after cycling, showing the difference in the reflection positions. The diffraction patterns were stacked for a better comparison.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Rietveld analysis of K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, which has a better crystallinity than K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O, revealed the presence of two layered structures in the material after cycling, namely a P3 form (space group <i>R</i>3<i>m</i>, <i>a</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;2.8489(3)&nbsp;Å, <i>c</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;16.9437(33)&nbsp;Å) and O1 form in a double quantity (space group <i>P</i>-3<i>m</i>1, <i>a</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;2.8524(3)&nbsp;Å, <i>c</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;5.6574(18)&nbsp;Å), refinement of experimental data is shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information). Analysis of the K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O diffraction data after cycling confirmed the presence of only a P3 form with the space group <i>R</i>3<i>m</i>, <i>a</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;2.8538(4)&nbsp;Å, <i>c</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;17.3612(67)&nbsp;Å. A difference between the two materials is highlighted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406384-fig-0009">9b</a>. Comparison of the data leads to two conclusions: 1) even if most K-cations are removed from the structure after cycling, some H<sub>2</sub>O molecules are still present, extending the interlayer space, 2) these H<sub>2</sub>O molecules apparently prevent the phase transformation P3&nbsp;→&nbsp;O1 during charging. Chemical analysis of both materials after 25 cycles pointed to the same Co:Mn ratio as in the pristine state, and the presence of both, Na and K. For the initial K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, the Na-content varied in different samples after cycling between 0.6 and 0.7 and the K-content was ≈0.4. For the initial K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O, the Na-content after cycling was slightly lower (of ≈0.5), and the K-amount of 0.4. Although we suspected that some KClO<sub>4</sub> admixture on the surface after battery operation could influence the results of ICP-OES, less Na-amount systematically measured for several K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O samples can imply a presence of some remaining H<sub>2</sub>O molecules in the structure and their negative impact on the cation exchange.</p>
            
            <p>Structural changes in K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O during the first two cycles in Na-cells were monitored using <i>operando</i> synchrotron XRD analysis (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202406384-fig-0010">10</a>). Immediately after starting the battery charge, the P3 form of K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> transforms to the O3 form, which is visible as the increasing intensity of the 104 Bragg reflection.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0056_R_d30505731e3159" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Chem. Mater.">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The O3 form seems to be stable during cell charge to 4.2&nbsp;V and discharge down to 2.1&nbsp;V; below this value, it transforms back to the P3 form. This transformation occurs almost abruptly, without any coexistence range of both phases.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406384-fig-0010"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/c7d9280e-cb41-4758-a218-2c05d6a1673d/adfm202406384-fig-0010-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/c7d9280e-cb41-4758-a218-2c05d6a1673d/adfm202406384-fig-0010-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/83bb655b-b177-41fc-8761-88146e4f9001/adfm202406384-fig-0010-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/c7d9280e-cb41-4758-a218-2c05d6a1673d/adfm202406384-fig-0010-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 10<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406384-fig-0010&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406384" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Counter plots of XRD data of K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (left) and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O (right) cathodes in Na-cells with the 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">M</span> NaClO<sub>4</sub> electrolyte, recorded in <i>operando</i>. The asterisks mark the positions of new reflections, which probably correspond to Na-rich phases.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Simultaneously, a new reflection at ≈4.2° 2Theta becomes more and more pronounced after an appearance in the first cell discharge. This reflection (marked as an asterisk in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406384-fig-0010">10</a>) corresponds to a Na-rich phase, which amounts increases with time. Therefore, two processes seem to proceed in the K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode upon electrochemical treatment in the Na-cell: a reversible P3&nbsp;↔&nbsp;O3 transition in the K-material and an irreversible formation of a Na-containing phase via cation K&nbsp;→&nbsp;Na replacement. The new Na-phase is electrochemically active as seen from shift of the reflection position. A similar P3&nbsp;↔&nbsp;O3 transformation was reported for potassium storage in the layered P3-K<sub>0.5</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> cathode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0047_R_d30505731e3230" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Adv. Mater.">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>In contrast, the K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O cathode demonstrates less structural changes during the charging and discharging the Na-cell. During the first cell charge, the composition of the P3 phase is varied as concluded from shift of main reflections. At the end of the charge, some new reflections start to appear (marked by asterisks), which intensities are growing, but 2Theta angle positions do not shift, meaning less change in the composition. Therefore, a two-phase reaction process seems to occur with negligible changes in the composition of the phases.</p>
            
            <p><i>Operando</i> XAS measurements of K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O cathodes in Na-cells on the Co K-edge clearly revealed a lower oxidation state of Co in K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202406384-fig-0011">11</a>), since the sample in the pristine state has a lower Co K-edge energy position of 7723.6&nbsp;eV in comparison to 7724.5&nbsp;eV for K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O. It is well established that the valence state of 3d transition metals directly correlates with the position of the absorption edge E, defined at <i>µ&nbsp;=&nbsp;</i>0.8.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0057_R_d30505731e3297" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Phys. Rev. B">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> A chemical shift of ≈2&nbsp;eV between CoO with Co<sup>2+</sup> and Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> with Co<sup>2.67+</sup> agrees with a chemical shift of 3&nbsp;eV, usually observed between absorption edge positions of oxide materials with Co<sup>2+</sup> and Co<sup>3+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0041_R_d30505731e3316" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Based on this assumption, we can conclude a Co<sup>3+</sup>- state in K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and a Co<sup>3.25+</sup>- state in K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O. The higher oxidation state of Co can also be confirmed by EXAFS analysis of the spectra, based on the structural models from NPD data: the refined Co-O bond length for K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> is 1.93&nbsp;Å, while 1.91&nbsp;Å for K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O, in agreement with the smaller ionic radius of more oxidized Co cations.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0048_R_d30505731e3364" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Acta Cryst. A">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Some examples of experimental and simulated Fourier transformations of Co K-edge EXAFS data for K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O materials are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a> (Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406384-fig-0011"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/8125c76d-d526-4a87-adb4-2118793097b5/adfm202406384-fig-0011-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/8125c76d-d526-4a87-adb4-2118793097b5/adfm202406384-fig-0011-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1c722f51-7c7b-4828-b60d-57ad80224261/adfm202406384-fig-0011-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/8125c76d-d526-4a87-adb4-2118793097b5/adfm202406384-fig-0011-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 11<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406384-fig-0011&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406384" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Selected <i>operando</i> Co K-edge spectra of K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (left) and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O (right) cathodes in Na-cells with the 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">M</span> NaClO<sub>4</sub> electrolyte, together with CoO and Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> reference materials.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The oxidation of cobalt ions in K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O can be understood in the following way. Upon air storage, K-cations react with H<sub>2</sub>O and CO<sub>2</sub> building the KHCO<sub>3</sub> phase. For the charge compensation reason, Co-cations in K<sub>0.5-x</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> must be oxidized, probably by O<sub>2</sub> from the air.</p>
            
            <p>During battery charge and discharge, Co is reversibly oxidized and reduced, as concluded from analysis of Co K-edge spectra, but the lowest oxidation state is always Co<sup>3+</sup>. Some selected K-edge spectra of materials in different states of charge are depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406384-fig-0011">11</a>. The interatomic Co–O distances, determined by EXAFS, reached 1.88&nbsp;Å in the charged state for both materials.</p>
            
            <p>Na-removal and insertion from/into Na<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.1</sub>Na<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> proceeds via a solid-solution mechanism, very similar to Na<sub>0.8</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> discussed in the previous work.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0051_R_d30505731e3513" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Energies">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Only the Co redox process was detected.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0051_R_d30505731e3518" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Energies">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0110">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202406384-sec-0110-title">3 Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>The strategy to enhance the alkali cations diffusivity with simultaneous mitigation of intermediate phase transformations through increasing the interatomic distance in layered Na-oxide materials (pillar effect) could be a promising approach to design materials with outstanding performance at high current rates. Here both main layered structure types, with the ABC…ABC and AB…AB oxygen arrangements can benefit. For example, a clear advantage of K-presence in the layered structure for Na-batteries was shown by comparison of the electrochemical performance of K<sub>0.7</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.7</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> nanomaterials:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0058_R_d30505731e3549" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Nano Energy">58</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> for 100 charge–discharge cycles, K<sub>0.7</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> displays a superior capacity of 134 versus 68&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at a current density of 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
         
         <p>However, such materials can exhibit an enhanced chemical activity, making necessary complex synthesis protocols and careful storage conditions. In the case of K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, its storage in air leads to fast intercalation of water molecules, subsequent elimination of K-cations from the crystal structure and their reaction with CO<sub>2</sub> and H<sub>2</sub>O. The H<sub>2</sub>O molecules penetrate between the layers of the layered structure. The Co-cations get clearly oxidized in K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O after storage in air in comparison to the water-free K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, which indirectly confirms the elimination of K-cations and insertion of neutral H<sub>2</sub>O molecules between metal-oxygen layers because of the charge neutrality. Further, battery chemistries play a crucial role in case of K-oxides, and especially the electrolyte formulations are very important. Thus, using K-containing materials as Na-cathodes results in a fast and pronounced cation exchange K&nbsp;→&nbsp;Na in the electrode, even prior to starting the electrochemical treatment. However, due to lower solubility of KClO<sub>4</sub> in organic carbonate-based solutions in comparison to NaClO<sub>4</sub>, a thin KClO<sub>4</sub> layer is quickly formed on the surface of the cathode and probably hinders fast Na cations transfer from the electrolyte solution to the bulk electrode, what is especially crucial at high current densities. Using NaPF<sub>6</sub> electrolyte solution instead of NaClO<sub>4</sub> might partially solve the problem of K-salt precipitation due to a higher solubility of KPF<sub>6</sub>. Nevertheless, the NaPF<sub>6</sub> electrolyte itself shows poorer characteristics during cycling at high cut-off potentials, providing a thicker SEI with prevalent C-F species on the cathode surface. Therefore, the electrolyte formulation must be optimized as a further development of the K-substitution concept for layered Na-oxides. The next point concerns to phase transformations in the cathode. Although water molecules between metal oxygen slabs prevent the phase transformation P3→O3 in the K-phase during the first several charge–discharge cycles, they seem to decelerate the reaction kinetics, which is especially visible in rate capability tests at low temperatures. Moreover, after prolonged cycling, water molecules in the layered material ensure that the O1 phase is not formed in noticeable amounts in the Na-containing material. After cycling, both K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O still contain some K-amount, similar to other K,Mn-oxides with the pillar effect reported in the literature.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0044_R_d30505731e3641" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Nat. Comm.">44</a>, <a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0059_R_d30505731e3641" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - Battery Energy">59</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Comparison of the electrochemical performance of P3-K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (and eventually of K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O) with Na<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>MnO<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> from the literature,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0037_R_d30505731e3676" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - J. Phys. Chem. C">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> existing only in the P2-type structure, points to improvements of cyclability with introducing the K-cations into the electrode system: 95% of the initial capacity was observed after 30 cycles in K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> in comparison to 67–68% in Na<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>MnO<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. However, the performance is still considerably lower than the performance of the Mn-free P2-Na<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. Here, the absence of Jahn–Teller Mn-cations seems to be an advantage. Moreover, a minor introduction of the K-cations into the cathode, leading to a slight increase of the interlayer distance, affects rather negatively the electrochemical performance, especially at lower temperatures and higher current rates. Therefore, a positive or negative impact of partial replacement of Na though K cations in layered systems strongly depends on the cathode chemistries. It could be beneficial for Mn-containing systems, to mitigate the structural strains, induced by the redox pair Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>4+</sup>, but it seems to have no positive effects for the systems without Mn. To date, the impact of K-substitution has been studied in the literature solely for oxide systems with the prevailing amount of Mn cations in the composition. As a next step to further evaluate the effect of K-substitution on the electrochemical performance of layered oxides in Na-batteries, (Na,K)Co<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials must be synthesized and characterized. Up to now, we did not succeed in the synthesis of phase-pure K<sub>y</sub>Co<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials with a layered crystal structure.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0120">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202406384-sec-0120-title">4 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In the present work, we elucidated the role of K-cations in the layered transition metal oxide structure on the electrochemical performance in Na-batteries. Therefore, four layered compounds, P3-K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, P3-K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O, P2-K<sub>0.1</sub>Na<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.8</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K-free P2-Na<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> were synthesized and comparatively studied. The K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O materials were synthesized for the first time and structurally characterized. K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> shows a strong affinity to water molecule intercalation, which occurs during several hours under ambient conditions with the formation of K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O. However, not only H<sub>2</sub>O intercalation, but also expulsion of K-cations by H<sub>2</sub>O molecules seems to occur, since 1) a prolonged storage of K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O in air leads to the formation of KHCO<sub>3</sub> as a secondary phase, and 2) Co cations show a higher oxidation state in K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O in comparison to K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, in agreement with the charge compensation requirement.</p>
         
         <p>In the electrochemical Na-cells with the 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">M</span> NaClO<sub>4</sub> electrolyte, K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O show at 25&nbsp;°C discharge capacities of ≈120&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1C current densities, which, however, decrease with cycling rather fast. The water-free K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> demonstrates better rate capability properties than the water-containing phase, reaching the 1C current density 80&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 25&nbsp;°C and 45&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0&nbsp;°C (vs 70 and 27&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively). It shows also enhanced electrochemical properties in comparison to P2-Na<sub>0.67</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> from the literature. In contrast, the K-free Na<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> with the same discharge capacity of 120&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1C exhibits much better rate capability properties with 105&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 25&nbsp;°C and 70&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0&nbsp;°C, both at the current density of 1C.</p>
         
         <p>In Na-cells, K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O suffer from a drastic structural transformation originating from the K→Na cation exchange, which is completed during the first several cycles. After a prolonged cycling, the O1 phase was found in K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, which is usually considered in the literature as detrimental for the electrochemical performance. Against expectations, the K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*0.5H<sub>2</sub>O sample with weaker rate capability properties did not contain O1 phase after cycling. The Na<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.1</sub>Na<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials show a solid-solution reaction mechanism upon cycling, which probably maintains their better rate capability.</p>
         
         <p>To sum up, we can conclude that the impact of K-cation introducing between transition metal-oxygen layers in the structures depends strongly on the material's chemistries: it may have a positive effect on the electrochemical performance in Mn-containing materials with a Jahn-Teller effect of Mn<sup>3+</sup>, concluded from the literature and our results on K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, but rather a negative effect for materials without Mn. However, this statement should be verified based on a larger amount of cathode systems.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0130">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202406384-sec-0130-title">5 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0140">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0150">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0160">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202406384-sec-0160-title"> Synthesis</h4>
                  
                  <p>K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> was synthesized using the Peccini route in combination with a solid-state synthesis. Stoichiometric amounts of Mn(CH<sub>3</sub>COO)<sub>2</sub>*4H<sub>2</sub>O (Aldrich Chemistry, ≥99%), Co(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>*6H<sub>2</sub>O (Merck co., zur Analyse), and 5 at. % excess of CH<sub>3</sub>COOK (Carl Roth, ≥99%), calculated for 2.5&nbsp;g of the end product, were dissolved in 100&nbsp;mL distilled water under stirring at 50&nbsp;°C. Afterward, 4&nbsp;mol of citric acid (VWR Chemicals) and 1&nbsp;mol ethylene glycol (VWR Chemicals) were added to the solution, which was heated up until a mixture of a honey-like viscosity was formed. This mixture was then transferred to a muffle furnace and heated up to 180&nbsp;°C for 2&nbsp;h to completely remove the remaining water. The obtained powder-like material was ground in a mortar, pressed to a pellet, put into a corundum crucible and annealed at 450&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h to burn out all remaining organics. Afterward, the grinding procedure was repeated. At the end, the materials were calcinated in air at 930&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h and quickly cooled down. To remove any possible moisture from the sample, the materials were ground and annealed at 250&nbsp;°C for 5&nbsp;h. Afterward, they were immediately transferred to an Ar-filled glove-box with oxygen and water content of less than 1&nbsp;ppm to prevent a reaction with humid air.</p>
                  
                  <p>Na<sub>0.8</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.1</sub>Na<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> were prepared using a solid-state route from stoichiometric amounts of Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> (Sigma–Aldrich, 99.99%), TiO<sub>2</sub> (Anatase, Sigma–Aldrich, 99.9%), Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (Sigma–Aldrich, 99.9%), and K<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (Sigma–Aldrich, ≥99%), according to the procedure reported elsewhere.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0051_R_d30505731e4071" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Energies">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The mixture of initial components was ground, pressed into a pellet and kept at 900&nbsp;°C for 15&nbsp;h in air followed by 10&nbsp;h at 600&nbsp;°C and rapid cooling to room temperature. After synthesis, the materials were stored in the Ar-filled glove box. Phase purity was checked using laboratory XRD analysis (STOE STADI P diffractometer, Co-K<sub>α1</sub> radiation, λ&nbsp;=&nbsp;1.7889&nbsp;Å). Rietveld analysis of the XRD data was performed using Fullprof implemented into the software package FullProf Suite.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0060_R_d30505731e4078" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Mater. Sci. Forum">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The chemical composition of the materials was confirmed by the ICP-OES analysis.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0170">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202406384-sec-0170-title"> Stability in Air</h4>
                  
                  <p>The reactivity of materials with air humidity was studied using in situ laboratory XRD analysis. For this, the samples were measured at the STOE STADI P diffractometer using Co-K<sub>α1</sub> or Mo-K<sub>α1</sub> radiation (λ&nbsp;=&nbsp;0.7093&nbsp;Å). Additionally, in situ gravimetric measurements were done for K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at room temperature. Here, an increase in the weight of the water-free sample was recorded over several hours, and the water content calculated per K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> formula unit was evaluated as a function of time.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0180">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202406384-sec-0180-title"> Thermal Stability</h4>
                  
                  <p>The thermal stability of materials was evaluated using thermogravimetry and derivative thermogravimetry analysis (TG-DTA), carried out under a dried air atmosphere with a heating rate of 10&nbsp;K&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> (STA 449F5, Netzsch).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0190">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202406384-sec-0190-title"> Neutron Powder Diffraction Studies</h4>
                  
                  <p>Neutron powder diffraction (ND) data were collected using a high-resolution diffractometer ECHIDNA at the Australian Centre for Neutron Scattering (ACNS), operated by the Australian Nuclear Science and Technology Organisation (ANSTO), Australia.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0061_R_d30505731e4133" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - J. Appl. Crystallogr.">61</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Data were collected on K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and K<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub>*xH<sub>2</sub>O powdered samples synthesized from the same batch. After synthesis at 930&nbsp;°C, half of the sample was additionally annealed at 250&nbsp;°C for 10&nbsp;h and immediately transferred to the glove box. The other half of the sample was stored in the air for 15&nbsp;h to ensure H<sub>2</sub>O insertion. Datasets were collected between 15 and 475&nbsp;K using incident neutrons of 1.622&nbsp;Å wavelength, for both samples. Rietveld analysis of the data was carried out using the FullProf suite.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0060_R_d30505731e4160" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Mater. Sci. Forum">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0200">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202406384-sec-0200-title"> Electrochemical Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>Electrochemical investigations were performed in two-electrode Swagelok-type cells using a VMP3 potentiostat (Biologic Instruments). Electrodes were prepared by pressing a mixture of the active material with Super P carbon (BASF) and PTFE (Aldrich) in the 80:10:10 weight ratio onto an aluminum mesh as a current collector. As anodes, sodium chips (aot battery, 99.7%) were used. A typical electrode mass was varied between 1 and 2&nbsp;mg. A glass fiber cloth (Whatman, GF/D), soaked with electrolyte, served as a separator. As electrolytes, either 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">M</span> NaClO<sub>4</sub> solution in a mixture of ethylene carbonate (EC) and propylene carbonate (PC) in the ratio of 1:1, with 5% of fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC), or 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">M</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> in the mixture of EC and diethyl carbonate (DEC) in the 1:1 ratio was used in the half-cell setup.</p>
                  
                  <p>Galvanostatic cycling with potential limitation (GCPL) was performed at different current densities in a temperature range between 0 and 40&nbsp;°C. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements were carried out in the frequency range of 1&nbsp;MHz–10&nbsp;mHz after open circuit voltage (OCV) during 3&nbsp;h and after charge–discharge cycling with 1C current density (removal and insertion of 1Na per formula unit in 1&nbsp;h) between 4.2 and 1.6&nbsp;V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0210">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202406384-sec-0210-title"> <i>Operando</i> X-Ray Diffraction Studies</h4>
                  
                  <p><i>Operando</i> X-ray synchrotron diffraction measurements were conducted at ALBA synchrotron, beamline MSPD (Barcelona, Spain). An eight-fold coin cell holder, connected to a Biologic Instruments potentiostat, was applied as described in the work.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0062_R_d30505731e4198" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - J. Appl. Cryst.">62</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> A wavelength of 0.4100(1)&nbsp;Å was determined by analysis of reflections of LaB<sub>6</sub> reference material. Alternatively, <i>operando</i> XRD measurements were carried out using a laboratory STOE STADI P diffractometer with Mo-K<sub>α1</sub> radiation (λ&nbsp;=&nbsp;0.7093&nbsp;Å) in a transmission mode. The experimental setup represented a single coin cell holder connected to a one-channel VMP3 potentiostat.</p>
                  
                  <p>For the characterization of pristine materials, the first diffraction pattern was recorded before starting the electrochemical measurement. Subsequently, the cells were charged and discharged at a constant current. Diffraction data were analyzed by the Rietveld method using Fullprof.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0060_R_d30505731e4212" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Mater. Sci. Forum">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Reflections of the Al current collector served as an internal standard during the measurements, while the refined lattice parameter of Al provided an independent control of the reliability of the obtained model parameters.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0220">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202406384-sec-0220-title"> <i>Operando</i> X-Ray Absorption Spectroscopy (XAS) Studies</h4>
                  
                  <p><i>Operando</i> X-ray absorption spectroscopy measurements at the Co K-edge were carried out at the ALBA synchrotron (NOTOS beamline, Barcelona, Spain). The samples were assembled in electrochemical coin cells containing Kapton windows. A multi-sample holder for several parallel <i>operando</i> measurements was used.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0062_R_d30505731e4230" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - J. Appl. Cryst.">62</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The measurements were done in transmission mode; as reference materials, CoO and Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> were employed. The data processing and analysis were done using the Demeter software pack.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406384-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406384-bib-0063_R_d30505731e4240" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - J. Synchrotron Rad.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202406384-sec-0230">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202406384-sec-0230-title"> Post-Mortem XPS Analysis</h4>
                  
                  <p>The chemical composition of the electrode surface after cycling was characterized for Na<sub>0.7</sub>Co<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> as an example by X-ray Photoelectron Spectroscopy (XPS). The measurements were carried out at a PHI 5600 CI (Physical Electronics) spectrometer equipped with a hemispherical analyzer at a base pressure of ≈10<sup>−9</sup>&nbsp;mbar. A monochromated Al-Kα as the X-ray source operated at 250&nbsp;W was used. Survey measurements with a pass energy of 94&nbsp;eV and high-resolution spectra with a pass energy of 29.35&nbsp;eV were recorded for each sample. To avoid contact with air, the samples after electrochemical cycling were transferred to the spectrometer using a PHI 04–110 (Physical Electronics) transfer chamber. The binding energy scale was adjusted according to the C 1s peak position of adventitious carbon at 284.8&nbsp;eV.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202406384-sec-0240-title"> Acknowledgements</h2>
